Compressive Pile Load Test 
Test Pile P-14 
FY19 MCON P-169 
Water Transmission Line 
Joint Base Pearl Harbor-Hickam, Oahu, Hawaii 
Dear Mr. Ching: 
In accordance with the project design requirements, a static compressive pile load 
test was conducted on a driven test pile (Test Pile No. 14) on May 19 and 20, 2020. This 
letter report presents the results of our field observations, test data, engineering analysis, 
conclusions, and recommendations. 
The static pile load test was conducted on a 16.5-inch octagonal precast, 
prestressed concrete pile. Based on the project specifications, Test Pile P-14 was cast 
with a length of 82 feet and instrumented with 12 vibrating wire embedded strain gages 
(Model No. VCE-4200) manufactured by Geokon. The embedded strain gages were 
installed in pairs at levels spaced at about 15 feet along the load test pile, with the first 
level at about 3 feet above the tip of the pile. The test pile was driven to a depth of about 
69.2 feet below the existing ground surface, which corresponds to a pile tip elevation of 
about -47.4 feet Mean Sea Level (MSL). The approximate location of the load test pile is 
shown on the Test Pile Location Plan, Plate 1.  
At the completion of the initial pile driving, Test Pile P-14 was sticking up 
approximately 13 feet above the existing ground surface, resulting in one level of strain 
gages above the ground surface. To accommodate the compressive pile load test setup 
and testing frame, the top 12 feet of the pile stickup was cutoff, resulting in the loss of two 
strain gages (one level), designated as SG-11 and SG-12. Strain gage locations within the 
concrete pile and the final depths below the ground surface after pile driving are shown in 
the following table:

Removed for Load Test Setup 
Test Pile P-14 was driven on April 22, 2020. The test pile was driven using a 
Delmag D30-32 hammer delivering a maximum rated energy of 75,438 foot-pounds.  
During the test pile driving, Geolabs maintained a record of the blow counts and field 
observations of the driving behavior. The test pile driving log is presented as Plate 2. 
As mentioned previously, Test Pile P-14 was driven to the tip elevation of about 
-47.4 feet Mean Sea Level (MSL), due to refusal condition, resulting in approximately 13 
feet of the pile sticking up above the ground surface.  Consequently, the top 12 feet of 
concrete was chipped off in order to provide sufficient space to fit the load testing frame.  
Therefore, the total length of the load test pile was 69.2 feet measured from the top to the 
tip of the test pile.  A multiplexer was used to connect the ten embedded strain gages to a 
Geokon Micro-10 datalogger, which recorded the strains in the embedment strain gages 
during the compressive pile load test.  
The test pile was loaded in general accordance with ASTM D1143 Procedure B – 
Maintained Test Procedure.  Test Pile P-14 was gradually loaded to a maximum test load 
of 484.5 kips in increment of 42.5 kips.  Each load increment was held at least 15 minutes 
or until the rate of movement was less than 0.01 inch per hour.  The maximum test load 
was maintained for at least 12 hours while the rate of movement was less than 0.01 inch 
per hour; otherwise, it should be held for 24 hours. 
Subsequently, the test load was unloaded in four decrements.  Each unload 
decrement was held for about an hour.  The final rebound reading was taken three hours 
after the test load had been removed.  Two dial gauges supported on two reference 
beams with mirrors and scales installed on opposite sides of the test pile were used to 
measure pile head displacement.  The reference beams were also independently checked 
for potential movement during the test by scales and level surveying.  The load test 
readings and the load-displacement curve are presented on Plates 3 and 4, respectively.  
The compressive pile load test results are summarized as follows.

Based on the shape of the curve of the compressive load test and the Davisson 
failure criteria, the 16.5-inch octagonal concrete pile did not fail at the maximum 
compressive test load of about 484.5 kips.  The strain changes in the ten embedded strain 
gages were recorded using a Micro-10 datalogger during the compressive pile load test. 
The printouts of the strain gage readings are presented in Appendix A.  
General information pertaining to the embedment strain gages, calibration sheet for 
the strain gages, and calibration sheet for the load cell are included in Appendix B. 
Hawaiian Dredging Construction Company Page 4
